They query replicas or views that cannot change production data. The same principle must apply to agents, but it is not enough to enforce this only at the query level."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"There are several reasons for this."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["First, SQL filtering is unreliable. Even if you block write statements, many databases still support queries that trigger full table scans. Constructs like ",["$","code",null,{"children":"SELECT INTO"}]," can introduce new tables, and functions can produce side effects."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Second, read access alone is dangerous. It can expose authentication tokens, PII, or operational metadata. This is why databases themselves do not rely on client-side query validation and instead implement safety through roles, views, and replicas."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Re-implementing parts of this logic in the agent layer with regexes or heuristics is both fragile and incomplete."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"agents-route-around-blocked-tools","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#agents-route-around-blocked-tools","className":"peer","children":"Agents route around blocked tools"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"An agent’s goal is task completion. Blocking individual tools does not mean entire classes of state changes are prevented. For example, if the agent finds that direct deletion within a database schema is blocked, it will reach the same outcome by putting together other allowed operations."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In this case, even though direct access to the tool is blocked, it doesn't prevent many other possible walkarounds that could apply undesired changes to the production system."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"agent-routes","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/agent-routes.0ad8ebd6.png","height":879,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAADCAMAAACZFr56AAAABlBMVEUqJyMxKiZa+aopAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAFElEQVR4nGNgYGBgZGRkgABGZCYAAI4ACrgmJ+8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":3},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In practice, this can include writing a script that performs deletion or just invoking a different tool that indirectly gives the expected outcome. This is not adversarial behavior. Instructions, allowlists, and approval dialogs influence behavior, but they do not define what the system is capable of doing."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"For that reason, safety cannot live solely inside the model. It must be enforced outside the model through OS permissions, roles, and tool interfaces. Access control is not a prompting problem. It's an infrastructure problem that will require explicit separation between reasoning and execution, with enforcement applied at deterministic execution boundaries."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"what-actually-holds-up-in-production","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#what-actually-holds-up-in-production","className":"peer","children":"What actually holds up in production"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"1-read-only-access-still-allows-irreversible-damage","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#1-read-only-access-still-allows-irreversible-damage","className":"peer","children":["1. ",["$","code",null,{"children":"Read-only"}]," access still allows irreversible damage"]}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["In one setup, we exposed production data to an agent exclusively through a read-only tool interface backed by a ",["$","code",null,{"children":"SELECT-only"}]," database role. On paper, this appeared safe - the agent could inspect data but had no explicit write tools."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"However, as long as the agent retained access to a general execution surface (shell access, runtime file system, or database credentials), it simply routed around the restriction, generating its own script and updating the database through an unintended path."}],"\n",["$","video",null,{"controls":true,"style":{"width":"100%","borderRadius":"8px","boxShadow":"0 4px 12px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.15)"},"children":[["$","source",null,{"src":"https://assets.docs.getpochi.com/agent-routes-around.mp4","type":"video/mp4"}],["$","p",null,{"children":"Your browser does not support the video tag."}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"We removed the execution surface entirely and enforced read-only access at the infrastructure level. This involved revoking database write permissions and disabling shell execution. Post this, the agent could reason freely but could no longer apply any changes."}],"\n",["$","video",null,{"controls":true,"style":{"width":"100%","borderRadius":"8px","boxShadow":"0 4px 12px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.15)"},"children":[["$","source",null,{"src":"https://assets.docs.getpochi.com/requires-human-approvals.mp4","type":"video/mp4"}],["$","p",null,{"children":"Your browser does not support the video tag."}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["Even when ",["$","code",null,{"children":"read-only"}]," access is enforced at the infrastructure level, production access still depends on human approval. Over time, these approvals tend to degrade into procedural steps. Auto-approve paths appear, reviews become mechanical, and the safety boundary weakens."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"As a result, granting agents direct access to production databases, even in read-only mode, is best avoided. Agents are non-deterministic by design, and production systems should not be exposed to that uncertainty."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"The challenge is that many legitimate tasks still require writes."}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"2-writes-must-flow-through-existing-deployment-pipelines","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#2-writes-must-flow-through-existing-deployment-pipelines","className":"peer","children":"2. Writes must flow through existing deployment pipelines"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Many engineering tasks involve backfills, schema updates, and data correction. All of these require write access."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Giving an agent write access to production data under these circumstances is rarely acceptable. A more robust pattern is to let agents propose changes, generate and test migration scripts, and iterate freely. But applying those same changes to production will still wait on explicit human approval."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"write-process","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/write-process.3ae10e09.png","height":879,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAADCAMAAACZFr56AAAABlBMVEUrJyMvLibjcTLyAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAE0lEQVR4nGNgAAFGRkYwAaZhAAAAqAAKFtZAMgAAAABJRU5ErkJggg==","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":3},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This mirrors standard engineering practice. It avoids giving production credentials to agents and ensures all changes are auditable and reversible."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"The tradeoff is slower iteration, because agents can’t validate assumptions against real production data. This is where isolated writable environments become important."}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"3-isolated-writable-environments-enable-safe-iteration","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#3-isolated-writable-environments-enable-safe-iteration","className":"peer","children":"3. Once the changes are ready, the same test and migration scripts can be replayed through the original production pipelines."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"iwe-system","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/iwe-system.a7db0288.png","height":960,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAADCAMAAACZFr56AAAABlBMVEUqJyMxLyzHW7dyAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAF0lEQVR4nGNgAAFGMAljMDIwMjIyMgAAAFEACKQmpX8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":3},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In practice, combining IWEs with gated production deployment yields the best results. With SSH and shell access, the execution surface becomes effectively unbounded unless similar infrastructure-level boundaries are enforced."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"why-shells-make-safety-undefined","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#why-shells-make-safety-undefined","className":"peer","children":"Why shells make safety undefined"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"A shell is a general-purpose programming environment. Once exposed, safety boundaries become undefined."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["An agent can use ",["$","code",null,{"children":"cat"}]," to overwrite files, using ",["$","code",null,{"children":"grep"}]," can exfiltrate secrets, and ",["$","code",null,{"children":"tail -f"}],", if used on the wrong file, can leak sensitive data indefinitely. far in this series, you’ve seen ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"$L6c"}],", what that ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"$L6d"}]," to make a prediction, and how these model ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"$L6e"}]," under continuous typing."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"With this, we’ve reached a point where NES can predict what edit should happen and when it should appear in the editor."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["In Part 4, we'll talk about how there is still one critical decision to make. ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Once a suggestion arrives, how should that change be presented inside a live editor?"}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Pochi’s NES is built as a VS Code-native feature, not a standalone IDE or a custom fork. This means previews must integrate with VS Code’s public APIs, performance model, and established interaction patterns."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["This introduces a core design challenge - to surface enough context for a suggestion to be actionable, ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"without disrupting the developer's flow."}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Designing a system that honors this is more than a matter of visual polish; it is a complex systems + UX problem. We’ll explore why this balance is so difficult for a native AI agent and the specific rendering strategies NES uses to achieve it."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"the-display-problem","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#the-display-problem","className":"peer","children":"The Display Problem"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Unlike conventional editor features, NES does not control where the user’s cursor is when a suggestion arrives. The editor is a continuously changing environment and does not function like a static canvas. Sometimes the user's cursor might be exactly where the edit belongs, or it can be twenty lines away, or the suggestion itself can be a huge change spanning multiple lines."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Showing such suggestions naïvely introduces new failure modes that are easy to trigger and hard to ignore. One experiences jumps in cursor position, abrupt viewport scrolls, or rendering large changes directly in the editing flow. In practice, these behaviors are often more disruptive than not showing a suggestion at all."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["This brings us to the most fundamental design question: ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"How do we show an edit without stealing the developer’s attention?"}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Answering that question requires understanding the VS Code interaction model."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"VS Code does not provide a built-in API for previewing LLM-generated edits. Instead, the editor offers different primitives for different kinds of locations and edits. These primitives are optimized for various interaction patterns, each with their own affordances and limitations. Some work well for cursor-local edits, while others are better suited for changes elsewhere in the file."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Understanding this difference is key. Pochi's NES does not render suggestions in a single, fixed way. Instead, NES relies on these primitives to create a balance between visibility and disruption."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"dynamic-rendering-strategy","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#dynamic-rendering-strategy","className":"peer","children":"Dynamic Rendering Strategy"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Rather than forcing all suggestions into a single representation, we designed a Dynamic Rendering Strategy offering the optimal visual experiences in different editing scenarios:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Suggestions that target ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"the current cursor position"}]," are rendered inline, flowing naturally into the user's typing behavior."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Suggestions that apply ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"off-cursor"}]," are previewed via an inline diff decoration, avoiding jumps in the viewport."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["For ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"large, multi-line block inserts"}],", a floating preview is used to provide sufficient context without disrupting the user's current focus."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This way, each path is deliberately scoped to the situations where it performs best, aligning it with the least disruptive representation for a given edit."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Let’s take a walk-through of these rendering strategies in detail and examine when each one is used, starting with the least disruptive case."}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"inline-completion","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#inline-completion","className":"peer","children":"Inline Completion"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"When an edit is positioned right at the cursor, the least disruptive option is to stay out of the way. In such cases, we render the edit inline, making it blend directly into the user's typing flow."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"To achieve this, we use VS Code's inline completion API. This approach works especially well for small, localized changes like autoclosing brackets, replacing a few characters, or edits that are directly made under the cursor."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image Part 4","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/nes-inline-completion-blog.a236fa9f.gif","height":1080,"width":2896,"blurWidth":0,"blurHeight":0},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"inline-diff-preview","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#inline-diff-preview","className":"peer","children":"Inline Diff Preview"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Because NES predicts the next meaningful edit across the file (not just at the cursor), many suggestions naturally apply outside the user’s current editing position. For example, while you are typing inside a function, NES may suggest updating a related import, adjusting a type definition, or fixing a reference several lines away."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In these cases, the cost of getting the presentation wrong is high. The user is forced to jump across the file, break context and interrupt their flow."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"To avoid that, we render the suggestion as an inline diff decoration. The text to be replaced is highlighted in red, while the new content is shown in green at the insertion point. This way, the user gets a clear preview of the change without moving the cursor."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image Part 4","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/inline-diff-completion-nes-part-4-blog.cdd15366.gif","height":1080,"width":2896,"blurWidth":0,"blurHeight":0},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This works particularly well for changes involving single-line updates or even multiple lines where each line is being changed independently."}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"floating-diff-image","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#floating-diff-image","className":"peer","children":"Floating Diff Image"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Because NES has the ability to propose structural edits, such as inserting a new helper function, refactoring a block of logic, or adding a multi-line configuration, it frequently produces multi-line suggestions that cannot be represented as simple, inline changes."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In these cases, the suggestion is no longer tied to the cursor’s immediate context, and the standard inline rendering stratergies do not suffice."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"At this point, the decision falls under either pulling the user away from where they’re working or bringing the preview to them. Since preserving developer flow is a core design principle for NES, we consistently choose the latter."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In order to make the suggestion appear near the edit target without moving the cursor, we generate a floating diff preview and render it as an image. The color schema of the suggestion will also stay consistent with the other solutions we discussed previously - red for deleted text, and green for inserted ones."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"VS Code allows extensions to attach image-based decorations. With careful layout and positioning, these decorations can be floated near the edit target and used as a diff preview. However, the editor does not render code into images, which means the preview has to be generated by the extension itself."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This required a small rendering pipeline:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Theme matching:"}]," Every VS Code theme is an extension with a standard JSON format. We parse the active theme, extract its token colour map, and match it to the user’s active settings so the preview matches the theme in the editor."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Syntax highlighting:"}]," VSCode includes a bundled ",["$","code",null,{"children":"TextMate"}]," runtime. We load the grammar for the current filetype, generate syntax scopes, and apply the same colouring rules that VS Code uses. This ensures that the rendered code maintains the same appearance as the code in the editor."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Image rendering:"}]," Here we use ",["$","code",null,{"children":"canvaskit-wasm"}]," to render the tokenized code into an image. To draw the code properly, we took the editor’s current ",["$","code",null,{"children":"fontSize"}]," and ",["$","code",null,{"children":"lineHeight"}],", drew each tokenized segment at the correct coordinates, then applied diff highlights (additions in green and removals in red). The final image is then surfaced using the decoration API."]}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image Part 4","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/floating-preview-nes-part-4-blog.faa6c6e3.gif","height":852,"width":3840,"blurWidth":0,"blurHeight":0},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This approach allows multi-line edit suggestions to appear near their target location while preserving cursor position and avoiding viewport jumps."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"conclusion-2","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#conclusion-2","className":"peer","children":"Conclusion"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Different kinds of edit suggestions need different presentation strategies, with the editor API playing a decisive role in shaping the final experience."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Rendering an NES suggestion ended up being less about displaying text and more about maintaining the reader’s attention. But incorporating them into an end-to-end real-time engineering system requires more thinking about real developer coding behaviour."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/cover-nes-part-3.8965694a.png","height":945,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAADCAMAAACZFr56AAAADFBMVEUhKCE1NCstLCVIQC+P6DbEAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAHUlEQVR4nB3IsQ0AAAyDMCD//1ypHo1abDij5AM4Af4AIIzDVVMAAAAASUVORK5CYII=","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":3},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"A code editor is a continuously changing space. Developers type, pause, delete, move the cursor, undo, redo, and essentially keep editing, often faster than any model can respond. Even a fast model call involves network latency, debouncing delays, server-side scheduling, and decoding / streaming time."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"If not careful, a request that was correct when it was sent can return a response that arrives a few hundred milliseconds too late. Which means now you end up with edit suggestions for code that no longer exists. This is something that’s termed “haunted” for being technically right but not at the right place."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/editor-stale-response-nes-part-3.b6187f22.png","height":1287,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAECAMAAACEE47CAAAADFBMVEUyLSIkKCA8NiMcHBmJFjhJAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAIElEQVR4nB3HwREAAAyCMND9d+5ZXgHVtiUB0CFRt98BAzIAIsPt520AAAAASUVORK5CYII=","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":4},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This means, in practice, a correct edit shown at the wrong moment is perceived as wrong by the user. So even with proper context and a good model, it is equally important to have the correct timing. Then only can the product actually feel useful without being distracting."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"But getting timing right is challenging, due to the ever evolving nature of the user’s editing state. To make NES feel real-time and helpful, we had to reason about what happens before a request is sent, while it’s in-flight, and after the model responds. This is what we call request management."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Let’s look at it in more detail."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"the-nes-request-management-lifecycle","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#the-nes-request-management-lifecycle","className":"peer","children":"The NES Request Management Lifecycle"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/lifecycle-prediction-nes-part-3.c208bea7.png","height":1287,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAECAMAAACEE47CAAAABlBMVEUzMCU/OCeM5oB7AAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAEElEQVR4nGNgwACMUAAXAQAAkAAJJD6x0AAAAABJRU5ErkJggg==","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":4},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Request Management of a NES prediction happens in three stages:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Before the request:"}]," waiting until the user actually pauses"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"While the request is in-flight:"}]," discard anything that becomes outdated"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"After the model responds:"}]," keep the suggestion alive if the user continues along the same trajectory"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["These map to what we technically implement as ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"debouncing"}],", ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"cancellation"}],", and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"speculative-prediction caching"}],"."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This structure helps bring the intelligent results (what we get with context + model) to users reliably, even as they type continuously. NES continues to run this loop as you type.\nLet’s take a closer look at how we handle timing at each stage."}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"debouncing-requesting-the-model-at-the-right-moment","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#debouncing-requesting-the-model-at-the-right-moment","className":"peer","children":"Debouncing: Requesting the Model at the Right Moment"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"The first question we had to tackle was, “When is the right time to send a request?” When a developer is typing continuously, a request on every keystroke has little value and is wasteful. At the same time, waiting too long would make the system feel unresponsive and slow. We had to find that sweet spot that lies in detecting the exact moment the user actually paused typing."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Most systems solve this with a fixed interval, (say, 100ms), but real-world typing isn’t this predictable. Instead, we decided to adapt the debounce interval based on how the user is behaving right at that moment."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"To achieve this, we made NES pay attention to a handful of lightweight signals."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["For example, typing a ",["$","code",null,{"children":"."}]," often means the developer is about to pause to access a method of an object,  so we get the signal to shorten the debounce delay. Whereas, if the user is continuously typing through a variable name, we stretch the delay a bit to avoid jumping in too early. And if the model’s recent response times have been slower due to network conditions, we account for that too, so suggestions land at the exact moment the user expects them."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/debouncing-nes-part-3.7b2433e3.png","height":1602,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAFCAMAAABPT11nAAAADFBMVEUWFhUfHhgjJR8yMjBzVIK4AAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAIUlEQVR4nCWJsQ0AAAiDKP7/s6kyEUBHQlBTuEILx0vXAgSOACq0I+UgAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":5},"basePath":""}],"\nThis way, the result is a debounce time window that changes with the user’s rhythm. It is short when the user has paused, and long when they’re in flow, all while making sure it never exceeds 1 second."]}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"cancellation-correctness-over-completion","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#cancellation-correctness-over-completion","className":"peer","children":"Cancellation: Correctness Over Completion"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Once a request is finally sent, the editor doesn’t stop moving. A user can continue typing, move the cursor, or undo and redo steps before the model has even started responding. When that happens, the original request becomes stale instantly."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["In such a case, we cancel the original request from the client-side, and in turn, the server propagates the cancellation, with any late responses being discarded without ever getting them rendered to the UI.\n",["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/cancellation-nes-part-3.31d7e84d.png","height":1083,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAECAMAAACEE47CAAAACVBMVEUyLSMfIRxEOSROeEe4AAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAGklEQVR4nGNgZGRkYAQRTAwMMAYTExOIBwMAAhQAGCJxHmoAAAAASUVORK5CYII=","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":4},"basePath":""}],"\nThis is a deliberate design decision that optimises and enforces correctness in a live, ever-evolving editing system. We would prefer that NES show nothing rather than something misleading."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["If you’re interested in how this works end-to-end, including streaming behaviour, we’ve written more about it ","$L7b","."]}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"speculative-prediction-staying-one-step-ahead-of-the-user","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#speculative-prediction-staying-one-step-ahead-of-the-user","className":"peer","children":"Speculative Prediction: Staying One Step Ahead of the User"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Traditional caching is straightforward. If nothing has changed, just reuse the previous response. In the case of NES, this helps to avoid duplicate requests. And to think about it, throwing work away all the time would be expensive if we didn’t balance it out elsewhere."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"But we go a step further. When the model returns an edit suggestion, we don’t just cache it for the exact context that produced it, but also speculate on the next few contexts the user is likely to enter."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Now, if the user continues typing along the same trajectory, NES doesn't need to call the model again and can continue serving the speculated suggestion. We call this speculative prediction."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"A speculated prediction remains valid as long as the user is essentially still typing into the suggestion and the surrounding context hasn't changed."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"It’ll be better to illustrate this with the help of an example. Suppose a user types:"}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/caching-a-nes-blog-3.c209745c.png","height":483,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAACCAMAAABSSm3fAAAABlBMVEUaGxcdKSC2At6HAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAEklEQVR4nGNggANGRkZGBgYGAAAoAAWtBtemAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":2},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"NES sends a request and gets the following suggestion:"}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/caching-b-nes-blog-3.f97a5ae9.png","height":915,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAADCAMAAACZFr56AAAABlBMVEUaHBkbJh6miQhyAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAFUlEQVR4nGNgZGBgZAADRhCAsMAYAACaAApMcq9dAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":3},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"If the user then continues to type, resulting in:"}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/caching-c-nes-blog-3.1e8a09b3.png","height":483,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAACCAMAAABSSm3fAAAABlBMVEUcHBkdKyF3lcStAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAEElEQVR4nGNgQAKMjIwMDAAAHgAEpm/UlAAAAABJRU5ErkJggg==","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":2},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["This user edit is part of the received suggestion. Therefore, the suggestion should still be displayed (unless the user has explicitly rejected it by pressing ",["$","code",null,{"children":"esc"}],")."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"By retrieving this result from the forward prediction cache, we can display the suggestion faster and reduce LLM request usage."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/caching-d-nes-blog-3.dc6c47d5.png","height":1146,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAECAMAAACEE47CAAAADFBMVEUbHRgiIRkpJxolNSMg0wCaAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAH0lEQVR4nGNgYmRiYmIAASZmZmZmRjCTgZEBxGCEAAAC1AAifcgbUAAAAABJRU5ErkJggg==","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":4},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Of course, if the user is not satisfied with the cached suggestion, they still have the option to send a new request to get multiple choices. In essence, forward caching helps accelerate the common path, improving the overall experience."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"conclusion-3","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#conclusion-3","className":"peer","children":"Conclusion"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"By the time a suggestion appears in NES, a lot has already happened. Debouncing decides when is the right time to make a request, cancellation makes sure outdated intent never surfaces in the UI, and speculative prediction lets us reuse good existing predictions when the user naturally moves through them."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"While you’d find these techniques are familiar in distributed systems, applying them inside a code editor was a challenge of its own. it is RL that is necessary to teach them what works. On the other hand, introducing RL in software engineering brings its own specific challenges:  data availability, signal sparsity, and state tracking. In this post, we’ll break down how recent works address these challenges."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"Reinforcement Learning is Changing AI Coding Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/rl-blog-cover-image.ac318676.png","height":1288,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAECAMAAACEE47CAAAAElBMVEUmLTE2QkQkJyYwMSwuNDk7SlI5s3xfAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAIklEQVR4nBXGtw0AAAzDMLn9/3KQhSA2lFeb1EC1ToFvnAMEqgBFxbZJ4gAAAABJRU5ErkJggg==","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":4},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"So far, the focus of RL driven improvements had been based on competitive coding. For example, in LeetCode-style tasks, the model works in a closed loop. It generally receives a clear problem statement and in turn, it generates a single, self-contained solution."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This means there are no dependencies involved, no files systems to navigate, and no legacy code that can break. It is exactly like solving a logic puzzle in isolation rather than understanding the engineering implications on the overall codebase."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"However, the field of Software Engineering (SWE) in real-world is fundamentally different. It is a stateful, multi-turn interactive problem. A day-to-day involves much more than just writing the correct functions. You often need to navigate a file system, check up on dependency graphs, run the proper tests, and interpret logs in case of errors. This implies, an agent effectively needs to maintain coherence across a long horizon of interactions."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Which is why RL is an ideal candidate for SWE since agent actions produce verifiable results. At the same time, it also introduces challenges that are not present in single-turn tasks. For example,"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Data Availability:"}]," We cannot easily simulate millions of environmental interactions like we can with math problems."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Signal Sparsity:"}]," Often, success signals appear at the very end of a long sequence of edits."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"State Tracking:"}]," Along with the static text of the code, the model must understand the dynamic state of the runtime environment"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Recent works from Meta and Moonshot AI surfaced how the industry is pivoting from general reasoning RL to domain-specific SWE-RL to address these challenges."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"the-data-problem","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#the-data-problem","className":"peer","children":"The Data Problem"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In order to learn trial and error, the standard RL requires an agent to interact with an environment. For coding, this means running a test suite or compiling code. As compared to verifying math proof, this simulation will be prohibitively slow and expensive in a real-world setting. Here, the engineering challenges arises to figure out how to bootstrap the entire learning process without being dependent on costly online simulation."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["Meta proved that you can bypass the online bottleneck by using the massive offline history of Github. In its recent work on ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"SWE-RL"}]," they talked through this approach instead of setting up a live sandbox for every training step."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"But offline data lacks a reward signal. For every historical Pull Request, you cannot easily go back in time and execute tests. SWE-RL solves this by creating a process proxy reward. They calculate the fine grained text similarity  between the generated patch and the actual developer ground truth solution instead of just checking if the code runs."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"Process proxy reward","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/swe-process-proxy-reward.69e3750b.png","height":1500,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAFCAMAAABPT11nAAAABlBMVEUqJyM0LyjG/bGAAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAG0lEQVR4nGNgZGRgYAATIAChGRmhAsgMBgYGAAGOABE3/Z+DAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":5},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Depending on how closely the generated format matches the human solution, the model receives a continuous reward. On the other hand, if the model generates an invalid patch format, it receives a penalty. This demonstrates that even before touching a compiler, you can teach a model complex engineering behaviours like navigating file structures and adhering to project conventions using static history."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"the-signal-sparsity-problem","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#the-signal-sparsity-problem","className":"peer","children":"The Signal Sparsity Problem"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Next, we have the credit assignment problem while facing online training within executable environments. That means it is difficult to indentify which step really contributed to the final success of the model and which step should get the reward. This reflects on software engineering as any agent can fail after 50 steps of editing and testing. Standard RL struggles to identify which specific step caused the failure."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["The ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Kimi-Dev"}]," paper addresses this through task decomposition. It treats software engineering as a composition of atomic skills: the BugFixer (editing logic) and the TestWriter (verifying logic) instead of training an end-to-end agent to solve the issue immediately."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Their solution starts with Agentless RL. They train the model specifically on these short horizon atomic tasks using outcome based rewards. They look for signals on whether the patch passed the test or did the test reproduce the bug. And since the tasks are scoped down, the feedback signal becomes dense and clear."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Kimi-Dev shows that with minimal additional data, a model having these pre-trained capabilities can be adapted to a complex multi-turn agent framework. This suggests that the most efficient path to autonomous agents is rigorous skill acquisition’s followed by workflow adaptation rather than brute force end to end training."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"the-state-problem-building-a-code-world-model","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#the-state-problem-building-a-code-world-model","className":"peer","children":"The State Problem: Building a Code World Model"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Coming to the final challenge, which is also arguably the most profound. Engineers generally do not just read code as text but also think about the execution loops in their mind. This involves tracking how variables change in memory and how functions interact between files. Meanwhile, since current code LLMs lack this internal compiler engine, they just merely predict the next token based on statistical likelihood."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["Meta ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Code World Model"}]," addresses this by fundamentally changing the training curriculum. They realized that waiting until the RL phase to teach execution dynamics is too late. The rewards are too sparse and the gradient vanishes on hard problems."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Instead, in the mid-training stage, they inject process supervision directly. To teach the physics of code, they constructed two massive datasets:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Python Execution Traces:"}]," With over 120 million examples, the model is trained to predict not just the next line of code, but also the exact state of runtime variables (the values in memory) after every single line."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"ForagerAgent Trajectories:"}]," Agents with 3 million trajectories that interact with a Docker environment to solve tasks."]}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This forces the model to internalise a Code World Model. By the time the model enters the final RL stage it is no longer starting from scratch. It already understands if I write X then variable Y changes to Z."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Consequently, the RL stage becomes a process of Goal Alignment. It uses sparse result rewards like passing tests simply to guide a model.  It already understands execution physics to select the specific path that satisfies the verification requirement."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"Goal Alignment","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/goal-alignment.bd10f8a2.png","height":1011,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAADCAMAAACZFr56AAAABlBMVEUuKiY0MSxBDjzTAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAFElEQVR4nGNgYGSAAiQGIyMDIwMAAFYABxixu7cAAAAASUVORK5CYII=","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":3},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"takeaway-moving-toward-verifiable-agents","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#takeaway-moving-toward-verifiable-agents","className":"peer","children":"Takeaway: Moving Toward Verifiable Agents"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["This progression from ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"SWE-RL (offline proxy rewards)"}]," to ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Kimi-Dev (decomposed skill learning)"}]," and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"CWM (execution-trace world models)"}]," outlines a clear engineering roadmap for the next generation of code models and agentic RL frameworks."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"We are seeing a shift from generic reasoning to specialized engineering. In our case, it’s the layer between when a user starts typing and when the model is called with a well-formed prompt. During that in-between phase, the system gathers and prepares all the relevant context the LLM needs before we make a model request. ",["$","br",null,{}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"As to why it matters, imagine simply sending the entire file to the model on every keystroke. Not only will the model become slower and noisier, but you’d get unstable predictions and over 20 model calls per second, rendering the whole experience unusable."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Instead, as previewed in the first article, we provide NES with three kinds of context:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"File Context:"}]," text, filepath, cursor position, and the region to be edited"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Edit History:"}]," record of recent edit steps"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Additional context from other files (optional):"}]," e.g., functions/type declarations that help understand the current file ",["$","br",null,{}]]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Each of these depends on clever filtering, segmentation, and timing - all of which happen in milliseconds during normal typing, as we’ll learn below."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"1-file-context-finding-the-live-region-of-code","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#1-file-context-finding-the-live-region-of-code","className":"peer","children":"1. We answer this by gathering three quick pieces of information from the VS Code API:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"The current file text"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"The file path"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"The user’s cursor position\nUsing this information, we compute what is called “the editable region”. ",["$","br",null,{}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Most editors record undo-redo steps on a word scale - for example, when a user inputs a sentence, an undo action will revert the last input word.\nIn our case, for building edit prediction prompts, we do this on a larger scale."}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Once we receive information on a user’s cursor position and tracking gets initiated, we create an edit steps list, where each step is an accumulation of several text change events. These tokens tell the model:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"What part of the file is editable"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"The user’s cursor position"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"What the user has edited so far"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"What the next edit should be inside that region only"}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Unlike chat-style models that generate free-form text, NES is trained to predict the next code edit inside the editable region."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Below is an example of how NES predicts the next edit:"}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"SFT conversion image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/sft-conversion-image.c0648ed8.png","height":1896,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAGCAMAAADJ2y/JAAAAD1BMVEUsJyMmIR8eGBs5LCwlFh+Oq7I4AAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAJ0lEQVR4nC2KQQoAMAyDNOn/3zxaJngRgfJRjNAJzeAkK17Wnbr7AwX5ADs58N3FAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":6},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["In the image above, the developer makes the first edit allowing the model to capture the intent of the user. The ",["$","code",null,{"children":"user_cursor_is_here"}]," token shows the model where the user is currently editing."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"NES infers the transformation pattern (capitalization in this case) and applies it consistently as the next edit sequence."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["To support this training format, we used ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"$La3"}]," and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"$La4"}]," as data sources. Initially, we considered both open-source and managed models, but ultimately chose Gemini 2.5 Flash Lite for two main reasons:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Easy serving:"}]," Running an OSS model would require us to manage its inference and scalability in production. For a feature as latency-sensitive as Next Edit, these operational pieces matter as much as the model weights themselves. Using a managed model helped us avoid all these operational overheads."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Simple supervised-fine-tuning:"}]," We fine-tuned NES using ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"$La5"}],", with no training loop to maintain, no GPU provisioning, and at the same price as the regular Gemini inference API. Under the hood, Flash Lite uses LoRA (Low-Rank Adaptation), which means we update only a small set of parameters rather than the full model. This keeps NES lightweight and preserves the base model’s broader coding ability."]}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Overall, in practice, using Flash Lite gave us model quality comparable to strong open-source baselines, with the obvious advantage of far lower operational costs. You might be part-way through a feature when a bug report arrives, someone needs a small refactor reviewed, or a documentation fix is pending. Most tools and workflows force these tasks to share one working state."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"So you end up switching branches, stashing and popping changes, resetting your workspace, and trying to hold the original task in your head. This is context switching, and it’s one of the biggest hidden costs in software development."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["We released ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Parallel Agents"}]," to remove that cost. Each agent runs in its own Git worktree, which isolates the task’s state from the rest of your work."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","div",null,{"class":"w-12/15 md:ml-8 *:shadow-xl/30 *:rounded-lg","children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"Parallel Agent","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/parallel-agents-changelog.5a32ed1e.png","height":1461,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAFCAMAAABPT11nAAAABlBMVEUqKiojIiIPdxgdAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAGElEQVR4nGNgYGRkYGAAYQwAFYTJMTICAADGAAh6lpJmAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":5},"basePath":""}]}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"A great example would be to run the same task with different models to pick the best response. Won’t that be a faster and much better experience - all within the same timeframe?"}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This is different from other existing solutions, which operate inside a single editor tab. In those tools, you’re effectively working in one tab at a time: switching tasks means switching the state of the same working directory and the same conversation."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["On the other hand, ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Parallel Agents"}]," in Pochi keep tasks fully isolated by running each one in its own Git worktree.
